<span class="display-name-link"><a href="/user/ur3310187/"\n>don_agu</a></span><span class="review-date">8 December 2005</span>\n            </div>\n            <div class="content">\n                <div class="text show-more__control">There&#39;s never been a character like &quot;Kitten&quot; on the screen before or an actor like Cillian Murphy for that matter. What a feast of a film! What a joyful race through a desolate existence dressed in smiles and hope and gratefulness. Neil Jordan&#39;s introduce us to this extraordinary real life character with the magical slant of a fairy tale. A lesson for all seasons. A unique portrait of a victim that behaves like a hero. The idea of victim doesn&#39;t even enter the orbit of his reality. How beautiful! I hope this marvellous film find its way to a large audience. I want everyone to feel what I felt. I was enthralled by the positiveness at the heart of its message. And if all this wasn&#39;t enough. Liam Neeson! Giving the best performance of his career as the most human of the imperfect humans that populate the planet. Do yourself a favour, put aside preconceptions and run to have breakfast on Pluto.</div>\n                <div class="actions text-muted">\n                    208 out of 230 found this helpful.\n fill="none"/>\n            </svg>\n                <span>10</span><span class="point-scale">/10</span>\n            </span>\n    </div>\n<a href="/review/rw1382512/"\nclass="title" > Neil Jordan returns to his best material: gender bending and the IRA\n</a>            <div class="display-name-date">\n                    <span class="display-name-link"><a href="/user/ur7759378/"\n>roland-104</a></span><span class="review-date">31 May 2006</span>\n            </div>\n            <div class="content">\n                <div class="text show-more__control">This spellbinding, tightly written, tightly wound, full speed ahead film is Neil Jordan&#39;s best work by far since his 1992 hit, &quot;The Crying Game.&quot; And, interestingly, in this new film, Jordan returns to exactly the same intertwined themes that marked &quot;Crying Game&quot;: the armed struggle of Northern Irish Catholics against the British Crown and gender bending.<br/><br/>Unlike the last minute revelations in &quot;Crying Game,&quot; however, here the protagonist&#39;s transsexuality is placed front and center from the getgo. Cillian Murphy gives a bravura performance as Patrick &quot;Kitten&quot; Braden, in a story set in the 60s and 70s. Murphy oozes sensual vitality and is a world class flirt, but he&#39;s also genuinely kind and compassionate toward everybody.<br/><br/>The story is divided into 35 brief, fast paced &quot;chapters&quot; following Kitten&#39;s life over several years, first in a village near Belfast, later in London. The musical score, which is extraordinarily good, is an eclectic mix of everything from 40s pop tunes to Harry Nilsson and Van Morrison. Good supporting turns are provided by Liam Neeson, Ruth Negga, Stephen Rea, Gavin Friday and Brendan Gleeson. My top rated narrative drama of 2005: grade 10/10 A.</div>\n                <div class="actions text-muted">\n                    61 out of 69 found this helpful.\n                        <span>\n served now!!\n</a>            <div class="display-name-date">\n                    <span class="display-name-link"><a href="/user/ur1270905/"\n>philip-ct</a></span><span class="review-date">5 March 2006</span>\n            </div>\n            <div class="content">\n                <div class="text show-more__control">This film is about a transvestite on one level, but it is also a lot more: it&#39;s about, belonging, being, loving and being loved. What could have been a one-dimensional caricature becomes a three dimensional movie in the hands of a good director like Neil Jordan, and actors such as Liam Neeson, Stephen Rea, and Cillian Murphy (who is magnificent).<br/><br/>Cillian Murphy imbues Patrick &quot;Kitten&quot; with growing dignity as he/she matures through the film, and at the end she has become a self-assured woman, who has &#39;found&#39; family, her mother and father, and a meaning in life.<br/><br/>The film does not shy away from the Irish-English conflict, either, and the prejudice directed against &quot;Paddy&quot; is appalling, reminiscent of &quot;In the Name of the Father.&quot; It is not for the faint-hearted, be aware! Costumes and music of the late 60&#39;s / early 70&#39;s are both equally impressive. There is an excellent soundtrack.<br/><br/>In all, I found the film quirky and uplifting; a friend with me pronounced it &quot;depressing&quot;. Whatever, it needs to be seen and Provo&#39;s an interesting view of the times in which the story is set. Judge for ourself.</div>\n                <div class="actions text-muted">\n                    65 out of 74 found this helpful.\n                        <span>\n                            Was this fill="none"/>\n            </svg>\n                <span>8</span><span class="point-scale">/10</span>\n            </span>\n    </div>\n<a href="/review/rw1252387/"\nclass="title" > Kitty, kitty, kitty\n</a>            <div class="display-name-date">\n                    <span class="display-name-link"><a href="/user/ur1406078/"\n>jotix100</a></span><span class="review-date">1 January 2006</span>\n            </div>\n                <span class="spoiler-warning">Warning: Spoilers</span>\n    <div class="ipl-expander ">\n        <div class="ipl-expander__container">\n            <div class="expander-icon-wrapper spoiler-warning__control">\n                <svg class="ipl-expander__icon expander-icon " width="12" height="8" viewBox="0 0 12 8" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg">\n                     <path d="M10.197 0L6 4.304 1.803 0 0 1.85 6 8l6-6.15" fill="#2572B3" fill-rule="evenodd"/>\n                </svg>\n            </div>\n        </div>\n    </div>\n            <div class="content">\n                <div class="text show-more__control">Neil Jordan&#39;s films are always a pleasure to watch. There are always surprises in the way he develops his movies, as he proves with &quot;Breakfast on Pluto&quot;, which the director helped adapt for the screen with the author of the novel, Pat McCabe. Mr. Jordan achieves another triumph in his distinguished career with this new movie that has a genuine and gritty look thanks to the excellent cinematography by Declan Quinn.<br/><br/>When young Patrick is left at the step of the small town&#39;s church, Father Bernard doesn&#39;t seem too surprised to find the young infant at his door. He is instrumental in placing the young boy with one of the town&#39;s women who brings up Patrick until he is a teen ager. It becomes clear young Patrick is a little girl trapped in a boy&#39;s body. He begins calling himself Kitten. His love for the outrageous makes him dress in a manner that he sticks out from the crowd. As such, he attracts the eye of a singer of a band who falls for Kitten and takes her to live in a remote part of the country. Alas, the romance takes a tragic turn because of Billy&#39;s involvement with the IRA.<br/><br/>Kitten always wanted to find the &quot;Phantom Lady&quot;, a nickname he gave to his natural mother, who moved to London after giving him up. As he arrives in the big city, Kitten discovers a world he never knew and in many ways, he thrives int the rich atmosphere of that swinging place at that time. The film is, in a way, a picaresque account of Kitten&#39;s road to maturity. His goal to find his mother doesn&#39;t happen until the end of the film. When the moment comes, Kitten is not resentful of the way he was left behind as he discovers that his mother has made a life for herself and her new reality.<br/><br/>The film is a delight because the work of Cillian Murphy. Mr. Murphy makes the delightful Kitten come alive. This is a tricky part to play and with the guidance of Mr. Jordan, this young actor makes the most of it. Equally excellent in smaller parts are Liam Neeson, Stephen Rea, Brendan Gleeson, Ruth Negg and Gavin Friday.<br/><br/>The brilliant collaboration between Mr. Murphy, the star, and Mr. Jordan, the director, pays off in many ways making this film the delight and fun it is to watch.</div>\n                <div class="actions text-muted">\n                    32 out of 40 found this helpful.\n                        <span>\n                            Was this review helpful? Just as the film is committed, so is Cillian Murphy committed to being the best Kitten he can, and he succeeds to an almost uncomfortable point, which I think is part of the storytellers goal.<br/><br/>Who does not want to be loved? Not many of us, and Kitten wants it more than most. Her journey to find love in whatever form it may take is both touching and harrowing at times. You cringe when she finds her self in certain situations, and you root for her to take charge of her life, but that is something she is quite unable to do for the most part of her journey.<br/><br/>While this story features the good, the bad and the ugly of the transvestite lifestyle, there is no judgment being made, it is presented as a simple fact of Kitten&#39;s life from nearly the first time you see her. That in itself is refreshing. There are stereotypes, but not presented in stereotypical situation, which is also refreshing.<br/><br/>I came away from this movie with a warm feeling in my heart for the character, the story, and the commitment of everyone involved in the film, it drew me in, it took me to places I did not expect, and it gave me a film experience you simply can not find every day in our cookie cutter Hollywood film world these days. My hat is off to all of you involved in the film. If you like something different, something unexpected, and something unusual made with a lot of love, this is the film for you.</div>\n                <div class="actions text-muted">\n show-more__control">Cillian Murphy is superb as an alien of sorts finding its way in our midst. Giving the other cheek as if it was nothing. The goodness, Cillian Murphy, finds in his character goes - I&#39;m sure - far beyond what the screenplay may have required. The goodness of his character feels private. A personal discovery. I hope I&#39;m not making the character sound sentimental, because he/she&#39;s not, far from it and that is one of the many surprises to be enjoyed in a film full of surprises. Neil Jordan had already confronted sexual identity in the brilliant &quot;The Crying Game&quot; he, as far as I&#39;m concerned, goes even further in &quot;Breakfast On Pluto&quot;. There is no confusion here, everything is blatantly true. Moving beyond words. A mesmerizing piece of acting and film making of the purest kind. data-vote-url="/title/tt0411195/review/rw1218765/vote/interesting">\n    <div class="review-container">\n        <div class="lister-item-content">\n    <div class="ipl-ratings-bar">\n            <span class="rating-other-user-rating">\n            <svg class="ipl-icon ipl-star-icon  " xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" fill="#000000" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" width="24">\n                <path d="M0 0h24v24H0z" fill="none"/>\n                <path d="M12 17.27L18.18 21l-1.64-7.03L22 9.24l-7.19-.61L12 2 9.19 8.63 2 9.24l5.46 4.73L5.82 21z"/>\n                <path d="M0 0h24v24H0z" film\n</a>            <div class="display-name-date">\n                    <span class="display-name-link"><a href="/user/ur0376119/"\n>Dougster-5</a></span><span class="review-date">18 November 2005</span>\n            </div>\n            <div class="content">\n                <div class="text show-more__control">I lived in London in 1973, the year that the main character in the film arrives in London from Ireland.<br/><br/>Breakfast On Pluto caught the tone of London in 1973 so well that it was like re-living the past. A past when friendships were mighty and strong; a past when London was a sexually liberated city; a past when people were so wrapped up in television that the London park system had to hire people to dress up like the television creatures called wombles.<br/><br/>But more than bringing 1973 back to life for me, this film showed me an amazingly resilient Irishman named Kitten. To the people who think that a 135-minute film is way too long, I would tell them to go see Breakfast On Pluto, because those 135 minutes just fly by. And they are 135 minutes of great acting, across the board.</div>\n                <div class="actions text-muted">\n                    115 out of 145 found this helpful.\n from Mr. Jordan\n</a>            <div class="display-name-date">\n                    <span class="display-name-link"><a href="/user/ur2078751/"\n>lrpulini</a></span><span class="review-date">3 October 2005</span>\n            </div>\n            <div class="content">\n                <div class="text show-more__control">I saw this on 10/2 at the NYFF-we got last minute tickets right up front. Neil Jordan was present at Q&amp;A-an absolute treat. The film was simply wonderful from beginning to end--charming, emotionally satisfying, delicately nuanced and very powerful. The acting was sublime, as in all Jordan films. Cillian Murphy is so impossibly gorgeous and yet so fearless and skillful an actor, who uses his physicality to his supreme advantage. The Irish gang of three-Gleeson, Neeson and Rea, who usually appear in Jordan&#39;s films, were superb and touching as usual. There were wonderful casting touches--Bryan Ferry as a sicko, Gaivn Friday as a gay rockabilly, etc. The film was audacious, swerving mightily between broad comedy and grim tragedy. The most arresting elements were the amazing customes and the choice of 60s and 70s songs, something Jordan discussed in detail during the Q&amp;A.<br/><br/>I urge all cineastes to catch this one-you will be amazed and deeply satisfied.</div>\n                <div class="actions text-muted">\n                    82 out of 105 found this helpful.\n                        <span>\n        </div>\n    </div>\n            </div>\n    </div>\n</div>\n<div class="lister-item mode-detail imdb-user-review  collapsable" data-review-id="rw1347416" data-vote-url="/title/tt0411195/review/rw1347416/vote/interesting">\n    <div class="review-container">\n        <div class="lister-item-content">\n    <div class="ipl-ratings-bar">\n            <span class="rating-other-user-rating">\n            <svg class="ipl-icon ipl-star-icon  " xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" fill="#000000" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" width="24">\n                <path d="M0 0h24v24H0z" fill="none"/>\n                <path d="M12 17.27L18.18 21l-1.64-7.03L22 9.24l-7.19-.61L12 2 9.19 8.63 2 9.24l5.46 4.73L5.82 21z"/>\n                <path d="M0 0h24v24H0z" fill="none"/>\n            </svg>\n                <span>10</span><span class="point-scale">/10</span>\n            </span>\n    </div>\n<a href="/review/rw1347416/"\nclass="title" > An Odyssey of a Visual and Emotional Feast!\n</a>            <div class="display-name-date">\n                    <span class="display-name-link"><a href="/user/ur3223254/"\n>gradyharp</a></span><span class="review-date">21 April 2006</span>\n            </div>\n            <div class="content">\n                <div class="text show-more__control">BREAKFAST ON PLUTO is now on DVD and perhaps that will garner the larger audience it deserves after its scant art house run on the big screen. In every way this is a tender, sensitive, sweet story, full of hope, faith, indefatigable courage and persistence that is embellished by a first class performance by the gifted Cillian Murphy.<br/><br/>Ireland, late 50s early 60s, and a child is left abandoned on the doorstep of the local priest (Liam Neeson). The priest hurriedly places the infant with a foster mother and we watch the little boy Patrick Braden slowly grow into a cross-dressing child with outsider friends, loathed by his adopted mother to the point where he is unable to cope with life as a lie and makes off to London as a transvestite gay man (now going by the name &#39;Kitten Braden&#39;). He hopes to find his birth mother and his search leads him through the dregs of London, the city that &#39;swallowed up&#39; his real mother, becoming involved with the seamier side of the city, jailed mistakenly, becoming an apprentice to a magician (Stephen Rea), a cabaret singer, etc until he finally makes the discovery of his beginnings - his true parents - and his journey to find happiness ends sweetly.<br/><br/>The entire cast of this long (over two hours) film is so fine that never for an instant does the pace of the tale let up. The cinematography by Declan Quinn is splendid, the costumes by Eimer Ni Mhaoldomhnaigh are some of the best recreations of the 70&#39;s on film, and the musical score by Anna Jordan mixes her own creations with the wonderful tunes from the era and the result is brilliantly integrated into the film. Director Neil Jordan adapted the screenplay from Patrick McCabe&#39;s fine novel and finds all the magic and makes it visual. But in the long run if we are unable to identify and care about Patrick &#39;Kitten&#39; Braden the movie would seem silly. Cillian Murphy is such an honest actor (having spent time pre-production living with transvestites about whom he speaks so tenderly in the featurette) and gives a multifaceted, glitteringly fine performance. This is a fun, entertaining, and important film. Highly Recommended for all audiences! Grady Harp</div>\n                <div class="actions text-muted">\n                    10 out of 13 found this helpful.\n                        <span>\n                            Was this review class="lister-item mode-detail imdb-user-review  with-spoiler" data-review-id="rw2831782" data-vote-url="/title/tt0411195/review/rw2831782/vote/interesting">\n    <div class="review-container">\n        <div class="lister-item-content">\n    <div class="ipl-ratings-bar">\n            <span class="rating-other-user-rating">\n            <svg class="ipl-icon ipl-star-icon  " class="point-scale">/10</span>\n            </span>\n    </div>\n<a href="/review/rw2831782/"\nclass="title" > Oustanding\n</a>            <div class="display-name-date">\n                    <span class="display-name-link"><a href="/user/ur13538926/"\n>Rectangular_businessman</a></span><span class="review-date">14 July 2013</span>\n            </div>\n                <span class="spoiler-warning">Warning: Spoilers</span>\n    <div class="ipl-expander ">\n        <div class="ipl-expander__container">\n            <div class="expander-icon-wrapper spoiler-warning__control">\n                <svg class="ipl-expander__icon expander-icon " width="12" height="8" viewBox="0 0 12 8" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg">\n                     <path d="M10.197 0L6 4.304 1.803 0 0 1.85 6 8l6-6.15" fill="#2572B3" fill-rule="evenodd"/>\n                </svg>\n            </div>\n        </div>\n    </div>\n            <div class="content">\n                <div class="text show-more__control">While Neil Jordan is mostly known for directing horror films like &quot;The Company of Wolves&quot; and &quot;Interview with the Vampire&quot; and also dramas like &quot;The Crying Game&quot; and &quot;The End of the Affair&quot;, personally I consider &quot;Breakfast on Pluto&quot; to be his best movie, being a notorious effort worth of recognition.<br/><br/>Cillian Murphy is simply excellent on his role Patrick &quot;Kitten&quot; Braden. His performance made the character someone believable and human and it could be easily considered the most impressive work of his entire career.<br/><br/>Part comedy, part drama, and with a couple of bizarre &quot;fairy tale&quot; elements, &quot;Breakfast on Pluto&quot; manages to be an honest and genuinely emotional story which never fails to deliver. <br/><br/>Brilliantly directed and with an awesome soundtrack, &quot;Breakfast on Pluto&quot; is one of those films that could be watched several times without losing any of its merits. It is funny, sad and heartwarming at the same time, but not in a conventional way. (At least, not in the &quot;conventional way&quot; of Hollywood movies)<br/><br/>In a time when apparently everything have been said before, honest and well made films like this convince me that cinema is not dead yet.<br/><br/>8.5/10</div>\n                <div class="actions text-muted">\n                    8 out of 10 found this helpful.\n                        <span>\n                            Was this review helpful? <a href="/registration/signin"\n> Sign in</a> to vote.\n                        </span>\n                        <br/>\n                    <a href="/review/rw2831782/"\n>Permalink</a>\n                </div>\n            </div>\n        </div>\n        <div class="clear"></div>\n    </div>\n</div>\n<div class="lister-item mode-detail imdb-user-review  collapsable" data-review-id="rw1191001" data-vote-url="/title/tt0411195/review/rw1191001/vote/interesting">\n    <div class="review-container">\n        <div class="lister-item-content">\n    <div class="ipl-ratings-bar">\n            <span class="rating-other-user-rating">\n            <svg class="ipl-icon ipl-star-icon  " xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" fill="#000000" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" width="24">\n                <path d="M0 0h24v24H0z" fill="none"/>\n                <path d="M12 17.27L18.18 21l-1.64-7.03L22 9.24l-7.19-.61L12 2 9.19 8.63 2 9.24l5.46 4.73L5.82 21z"/>\n                <path d="M0 0h24v24H0z" fill="none"/>\n            </svg>\n                <span>10</span><span class="point-scale">/10</span>\n            </span>\n    </div>\n<a href="/review/rw1191001/"\nclass="title" > Breakfast on Pluto is amazing\n</a>            <div class="display-name-date">\n                    <span class="display-name-link"><a href="/user/ur7216365/"\n>Skstar1723</a></span><span class="review-date">10 October 2005</span>\n            </div>\n            <div class="content">\n                <div class="text show-more__control">This film is fabulous- and has nothing to do with the solar system (haha!) Cillian Murphy is AMAZING in his complicated role as a trans-sexual man growing up in Ireland in the 1970&#39;s and his quest to find what he wants in his life. (Do not judge Mr. Murphy&#39;s acting skills from just watching Batman Begins or Red Eye this level of acting falls more in the type of his earlier works such as On the Edge and Disco Pigs) Liam Neeson, Stephen Rea, and Brandon Gleeson are far more than excellent in supporting roles. This film is dependent on its star (Mr. Murphy) and he shines. The themes in this film are universal. Even while the story is sad and the situation the main character- Kitten-finds herself in are very sad, it somehow always becomes funny. The interaction between Kitten and the people around her is fascinating, funny and true-to-life. Mr. Murphy is amazing and deserves and Academy Award for his stunning and flawless portrayal of such a complicated character. It is fabulous!!! Don&#39;t want to spoil anything about the plot but if anyone has read the book DO NOT expect the same situations or ending.This film is tender, sweet, funny, has an amazing script and has actors that made this (to some) far-fetched (not to me or anyone I know but one could have that impression) fairy-tale like story excellent. If you strip away the complicated details of this trans-sexual Irish male and his travels during the 70&#39;s you can find the root, universal story of a young person looking for love.</div>\n </div>\n            </div>\n        </div>\n        <div class="clear"></div>\n    </div>\n    <div class="gradient-expander hidden show-more">\n        <div class="gradient-container show-more__control"></div>\n            <div class="gradient-footer">\n    <div class="ipl-expander ">\n        <div class="ipl-expander__container">\n            <div class="expander-icon-wrapper show-more__control">\n                <svg class="ipl-expander__icon expander-icon " width="12" height="8" viewBox="0 0 12 8" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg">\n                     <path d="M10.197 0L6 4.304 1.803 0 0 1.85 6 8l6-6.15" fill="#2572B3" fill-rule="evenodd"/>\n                </svg>\n            </div>\n        </div>\n    </div>\n            </div>\n    </div>\n</div>\n<div class="lister-item mode-detail imdb-user-review  collapsable" data-review-id="rw1256869" data-vote-url="/title/tt0411195/review/rw1256869/vote/interesting">\n    <div class="review-container">\n        <div class="lister-item-content">\n    <div class="ipl-ratings-bar">\n            <span class="rating-other-user-rating">\n            <svg class="ipl-icon ipl-star-icon  " xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" fill="#000000" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" width="24">\n                <path d="M0 0h24v24H0z" fill="none"/>\n                <path d="M12 17.27L18.18 21l-1.64-7.03L22 9.24l-7.19-.61L12 2 9.19 8.63 2 9.24l5.46 4.73L5.82 21z"/>\n                <path d="M0 0h24v24H0z" fill="none"/>\n            </svg>\n                <span>8</span><span class="point-scale">/10</span>\n            </span>\n    </div>\n<a href="/review/rw1256869/"\nclass="title" > A New Candide Takes the Irish Troubles in High-Heeled Stride\n</a>            <div class="display-name-date">\n                    <span class="display-name-link"><a href="/user/ur2042633/"\n>noralee</a></span><span class="review-date">30 December 2005</span>\n            </div>\n            <div class="content">\n                <div class="text show-more__control">If Candide had been born a trannie Irishman from the 1960&#39;s through Thacherite England, he would be Cillian Murphy in &quot;Breakfast on Pluto.&quot; <br/><br/>Neil Jordan draws on several genres to create an original view point of politics, music and human relationships -- takes on &quot;the troubles&quot; from &quot;Bloody Sunday&quot; and Jim Sheridan&#39;s films; the cultural changes in the period like Milos Forman&#39;s &quot;Hair&quot; and &quot;Forest Gump&quot;; drag queens from &quot;The Adventures of Priscilla, Queen of the Desert&quot; and &quot;The Naked Civil Servant&quot; and the gender-bending combination in his own &quot;The Crying Game.&quot;<br/><br/>But the story, direction and most of all the central performance create a complete person at a specific time that has renewed contemporary relevance. Whereas Felicity Huffman&#39;s transsexual in &quot;Transamerica&quot; just wants to disappear into normalness, Murphy&#39;s &quot;Patrick/Kitten Braden&quot; eschews the frequent importuning to be serious and wants from childhood to live his fantasies to make them real despite a world demanding either/or, with us or against us. This is the first film I can think of with no revelation of childhood sexual abuse for such a character, but rather an orphan&#39;s lack of parental love from birth.<br/><br/>Jordan marvelously pulls off the trick of seamlessly integrating for the viewer the gritty, tumultuous reality with &quot;Kitten&quot;s amusing talent for turning a sordid life into the best of all possible worlds as a romantic musical romantic fantasy. We see this world both from &quot;Kitten&quot;s perspective, complete with talking robins and sardonic autobiographical chapter headings that I presume were carried over from Pat McCabe&#39;s novel, as he co-wrote the script, and the reactions of friends and enemies, as &quot;Patrick/Kitten&quot; goes from the frying pan into the fire (perhaps too many times) amidst political, cultural and violent turmoil. <br/><br/>One of the continuing themes is no matter what worlds &quot;Kitten&quot; picaresquely glides through, from a small town to Dublin to rock &#39;n&#39; roll to IRA fighters to cops to nightclubs to London streets and more, homophobia trumps every other hatred that any one has for any other person, place, thing, religion or philosophy. This is adroitly illustrated when &quot;Kitten&quot; becomes enamored of a glam rock bar band, led by a charismatic Gavin Friday, and pushes the boundaries of that gender-bending performance art too far for straight guys&#39; comfort. Rocker Bryan Ferry also has a small, but non-musical role, as one of a string of many, many older men, some down right creepy, attracted to &quot;Kitten&quot; for good or ill in a distorted Oedipal mirror.<br/><br/>While &quot;Kitten&quot; doesn&#39;t actually say she is dependent on the kindness of strangers, it is a relief when now and again friends rescue her when she seems incapable of either common sense or self-esteem. Occasionally, &quot;Kitten&quot; does display some perspicacity and even maturity to reveal sanity and intelligence, as well as considerable artistic creativity, behind those wide-eyed baby blues, such as when she explains the layers of meaning behind the title and a pro-life theology that embraces all differences to find family, as well as finally dealing with parent issues.<br/><br/>Murphy&#39;s performance is simply astounding. I&#39;ve used gendered pronouns to indicate when the charming hunk from &quot;Girl With Pearl Earring&quot; or &quot;interMission&quot; or &quot;Red Eye&quot; completely becomes a woman throughout his body, no matter the camera angles, like no other straight male actor before has ever become a male to female transsexual on screen (Lee Pace&#39;s performance in &quot;A Soldier&#39;s Girl&quot; is the closest comparison). &quot;Kitten&quot; can be annoying, but she is always a real person, not a guy in drag.<br/><br/>The supporting cast is wonderfully atmospheric, particularly the lesser-known players Ruth Negga and Laurence Kinlan as &quot;Kitten&quot;s life-long friends and Ian Hart as an aggressive cop turned protector.<br/><br/>The Brit and Irish pop music selections on the soundtrack are brilliant. About half are unfamiliar to American audiences, including cover versions of others&#39; hits. The songs are perfectly selected for either lyrics or period evocation or rhythm or emotion, such as two Van Morrison tunes (&quot;Madame George&quot; and &quot;Cypress Avenue&quot;), for additional commentary on the action. It&#39;s hard not to hum along.<br/><br/>A warning to American audiences that the Irish brogues are quite thick; I&#39;d welcome seeing the film with not just the robins subtitled. This is exacerbated by Murphy&#39;s adopted feminine voice and swallowed cadence, which not only can get irritating, but seemed under-miked or not post-dubbed. I sympathized when cops were trying to shake him out of these mannerisms. <br/><br/>The extremely long credits at the end would seem to indicate some union feather bedding in exchange for the location shooting financial benefits.</div>\n                <div class="actions text-muted">\n                    11 out of 15 found this helpful.\n                        <span>\n        </div>\n    </div>\n            </div>\n    </div>\n</div>\n<div class="lister-item mode-detail imdb-user-review  collapsable" data-review-id="rw4259964" data-vote-url="/title/tt0411195/review/rw4259964/vote/interesting">\n    <div class="review-container">\n        <div class="lister-item-content">\n    <div class="ipl-ratings-bar">\n            <span class="rating-other-user-rating">\n            <svg class="ipl-icon ipl-star-icon  " xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" fill="#000000" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" width="24">\n fill="none"/>\n            </svg>\n                <span>9</span><span class="point-scale">/10</span>\n            </span>\n    </div>\n<a href="/review/rw4259964/"\nclass="title" > So good, one can hardly fault it.\n</a>            <div class="display-name-date">\n                    <span class="display-name-link"><a href="/user/ur2263198/"\n>paulclaassen</a></span><span class="review-date">30 July 2018</span>\n            </div>\n            <div class="content">\n                <div class="text show-more__control">Cillian Murphy is once again excellent in this coming of age comedy drama. I loved the soundtrack, as well, as the music was obviously very cleverly and carefully chosen. I found the film so awesome that I can&#39;t really fault it in any way. The humor is really funny, the drama is tense and there&#39;s even action and adventure thrown in the mix. The photography and unique visual style was also very good, as was the dialogue. Director Neil Jordan had a wonderful vision for the film.</div>\n                <div class="actions text-muted">\n                    5 out of 6 found this helpful.\n                        <span>\n class="ipl-expander__container">\n            <div class="expander-icon-wrapper show-more__control">\n                <svg class="ipl-expander__icon expander-icon " width="12" height="8" viewBox="0 0        </div>\n    </div>\n            </div>\n    </div>\n</div>\n<div class="lister-item mode-detail imdb-user-review  with-spoiler" data-review-id="rw1347006" data-vote-url="/title/tt0411195/review/rw1347006/vote/interesting">\n    <div class="review-container">\n        <div class="lister-item-content">\n    <div class="ipl-ratings-bar">\n            <span class="rating-other-user-rating">\n            <svg class="ipl-icon ipl-star-icon  " xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" fill="#000000" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" width="24">\n                <path d="M0 0h24v24H0z" fill="none"/>\n                <path d="M12 17.27L18.18 21l-1.64-7.03L22 9.24l-7.19-.61L12 2 9.19 8.63 2 9.24l5.46 4.73L5.82 21z"/>\n                <path d="M0 0h24v24H0z" fill="none"/>\n            </svg>\n                <span>10</span><span class="point-scale">/10</span>\n            </span>\n    </div>\n<a href="/review/rw1347006/"\nclass="title" > Little Boy Lost -- Little Girl Found\n</a>            <div class="display-name-date">\n                    <span class="display-name-link"><a href="/user/ur0384847/"\n>nycritic</a></span><span class="review-date">20 April 2006</span>\n            </div>\n                <span class="spoiler-warning">Warning: Spoilers</span>\n    <div class="ipl-expander ">\n        <div class="ipl-expander__container">\n            <div class="expander-icon-wrapper spoiler-warning__control">\n                <svg class="ipl-expander__icon expander-icon " width="12" height="8" viewBox="0 0 12 8" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg">\n                     <path d="M10.197 0L6 4.304 1.803 0 0 1.85 6 8l6-6.15" fill="#2572B3" fill-rule="evenodd"/>\n                </svg>\n            </div>\n        </div>\n    </div>\n            <div class="content">\n                <div class="text show-more__control">Some of the world&#39;s strongest people aren&#39;t the ones who display the biggest muscles and drag airplanes through their teeth while grunting and shrieking like banshees, but the most unassuming ones, whom you and I would take for granted and even pity them as they wander the streets of any major city, alone, looking for a niche in a world that would certainly kick them to death at the slightest chance. I&#39;ve always admired the subtle but iron strength that such people display because put through the most awful, degrading of circumstances -- such that you and I would cringe at -- they walk right through them, seemingly in denial but really unscathed, letting every ounce of baggage go and never looking back as they reach their final destination.<br/><br/>Neil Jordan&#39;s BREAKFAST ON PLUTO has to be, bar none, one of the most under-seen and under-appreciated movies of 2005. Why it didn&#39;t receive a wider distribution is probably a mishandling of its target audience -- plus, TRANSAMERICA was already basking in the lion&#39;s share of its movie-going audience and a favorite for most awards. The story of Patrick (Patricia) &quot;Kitten&quot; Braden, his abandonment by his mother at the doors of a church run by Father Bernard, his coming into an awareness that he would rather be a woman than a man at a very early age even when the mere suggestion drives his adoptive mother and older sister into fits of rage, and his/her subsequent escape into an dangerous world in search of the biological mother who keeps on appearing like a ghost and who in Kitten&#39;s mind looks like Mitzi Gaynor, couldn&#39;t be more well written than it is here.<br/><br/>Treated in chapters, it does have a strong parallel to the works of Charles Dickens (and no, I&#39;m not agreeing with the general consensus -- watch the movie and if you&#39;ve read any of his works you&#39;ll also have to agree there is a little more than a passing similarity to Dickens&#39; universe) with the appearance of extremely shady characters in Kitten&#39;s trek throughout London as she tries to reconnect with her mother. Weaving itself in and out of Kitten&#39;s life are the IRA, but this seems to be more circumstantial than essential to Kitten&#39;s character because she couldn&#39;t be less interested in rifles or bombs or their plight even when the people she associates with -- due to chance -- are. There&#39;s an extremely funny scene when after Kitten tanks as a rock chick because the band deems her an act killer and a target for homophobes, the leader of the band takes a liking to her, brings her to his trailer in the middle of nowhere, where once she decides to clean it up she finds a huge arsenal of rifles of all shapes and sizes and decides to dispose of them later, an act that almost causes her to get killed. Later on, she inexplicably winds up being a suspect in the bombing of a disco, but this is less due to her transvestism and more to her Irishness.<br/><br/>Despite a film about someone in the outer reaches of acceptance, there is surprisingly little homophobia in BREAKFAST ON PLUTO. The violence Kitten finds on the streets is again circumstantial -- anyone working the streets is subject to meeting the weirdest, creepiest folk and Kitten seems to attract them like flies. It&#39;s actually a relief when the same policeman who at first tried to wrestle any truth to her &quot;involvement&quot; with the IRA sees how she doesn&#39;t belong in the streets and takes her to a local peep show where she finally finds some order in her chaotic life and the woman inside her comes out in full bloom. As an added irony, this is exactly when she learns of her biological mother, but like the boy in &quot;The Alchemist&quot;, finding her mother is anti-climactic. It&#39;s been a trick throughout the entire movie. She never needed this reaffirmation of her own self -- she was always there.<br/><br/>It takes a lot of steel to play this kind of role and not many actors, so dependent they are on their perception of masculinity (itself a form of vanity and insecurity), can pull it off so convincingly. You will never see a Tom Cruise or a Mel Gibson do this sort of character -- perish the thought! Cillian Murphy, so vicious in RED EYE, does a complete left turn, and not only becomes Kitten but disappears completely into her femininity somewhat reminiscent of Dusty Springfield who continually sings in the background her &quot;Windmills of your Mind&quot;. It&#39;s such a moving performance that far exceeds Dustin Hoffman&#39;s in TOOTSIE and even Johnny Depp&#39;s in ED WOOD because it&#39;s not a one-note joke. Kitten is a man in search of his inner woman, knowing he is &quot;way out there&quot;, not caring one bit to play it stealth (as many transgendered do), who stands up to his existence as a she and finds her own acceptance, even when the world may not always embrace it.</div>\n                <div class="actions text-muted">\n                    11 out of 15 found this helpful.\n                        <span>\n                            Was this review helpful? <a href="/registration/signin"\n> Sign in</a> to vote.\n                        </span>\n                        <br/>\n                    <a href="/review/rw1347006/"\n>Permalink</a>\n                </div>\n            </div>\n        </div>\n        <div class="clear"></div>\n    </div>\n</div>\n<div class="lister-item mode-detail imdb-user-review  collapsable" data-review-id="rw1496240" data-vote-url="/title/tt0411195/review/rw1496240/vote/interesting">\n    <div class="review-container">\n        <div class="lister-item-content">\n    <div class="ipl-ratings-bar">\n            <span class="rating-other-user-rating">\n            <svg class="ipl-icon ipl-star-icon  " xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" fill="#000000" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" width="24">\n                <path d="M0 0h24v24H0z" fill="none"/>\n                <path d="M12 17.27L18.18 21l-1.64-7.03L22 9.24l-7.19-.61L12 2 9.19 8.63 2 9.24l5.46 4.73L5.82 21z"/>\n                <path d="M0 0h24v24H0z" fill="none"/>\n            </svg>\n                <span>8</span><span class="point-scale">/10</span>\n            </span>\n    </div>\n<a href="/review/rw1496240/"\nclass="title" > The Crying Game meets Velvet Goldmine meets... Cillian Murphy!\n</a>            <div class="display-name-date">\n                    <span class="display-name-link"><a href="/user/ur5513934/"\n>Flagrant-Baronessa</a></span><span class="review-date">13 October 2006</span>\n            </div>\n            <div class="content">\n                <div class="text show-more__control">It is admirable that a film of such tragic content can manage both accessible and enjoyable. In the front row for the &#39;tragic&#39; part is Kitten, a flamboyant, high-spirited transvestite who falls prey to prostitution and accusations of terrorism in Britain during the late 1960&#39;s. In the enjoyable end are the film&#39;s layered performances, fluent narration and, arguably its goldmine, the music...<br/><br/>The opening of &#39;Breakfast on Pluto&#39; sees a lively Cillian Murphy strut down the street to Sugar Baby Love by the Rubettes, with long blonde hair, red lipstick and a killer dress, playfully exchanging sass with onlookers and flirting with life. He is exuding courage. Cut to a bleak small Irish town on the border and a young woman leaving her baby outside the Bishop&#39;s door in a basket. The baby is Kitten and the bishop is Liam Neeson, whom upon discovering this new &#39;gift&#39; adopts a confused, troubled expression that he wears well for the rest of the film.<br/><br/>Where the good ol&#39; Bishop stays the same \xc2\x96 patient but troubled \xc2\x96 Kitten shifts onto a path that undoubtedly deviates from the strict conventions of the Irish community; he develops a fondness for cross-dressing in ladies&#39; clothes, writing racy stories and expressing himself creatively. Walking around in an idealist bubble of dreams while being harshly raised as a &#39;bastard&#39; child, Kitten&#39;s bubble bursts eventually and he runs off seeking greener pastures in London where he ultimately resorts to fully-fledged prostitution.<br/><br/>Although I am no member of the Cillian Murphy camp, I credit where credit is due and this film is a showcase for his unique talent. I say &#39;unique&#39; since realism is typically sought from actors today and Murphy embodies the opposite \xc2\x96 he is theatrical, over-the-top, colourful and flamboyant which is why he fits the part of a transvestite so well. His character, Kitten, stands up for what he believes in and when faced with injustice \xc2\x96 such as false accusations for IRA bombings \xc2\x96 he indulges in music, writing and art, descending into his own mind and never once letting the bitterness overcome him. The soundtrack to &#39;Pluto&#39; is nothing short of remarkable, sewing together the narrative with deft strokes. It is simply peppered with 1960&#39;s/1970&#39;s gems.<br/><br/>Yet the film&#39;s heaviest weapon in its arsenal is contrast, a device that Neil Jordon clearly has wielded to perfection here. One minute it is bursting with hippie music \xc2\x96 a sprawling surge of contemporary flair and fury that takes the form of fashion, music and lifestyle. The next minute it zooms back in on the bleak little Irish town making it overtly clear to the reader why Kitten fled his native town for London in the first place. Yet there&#39;s that familiarity about it, and Liam Neeson... needless to say, Pluto delicately juxtaposes the life in Ireland with the life in London during this era. In the portrayal of the latter, it aptly balances tragedy with comedy, funny with grave, bleak with colourful. It is a gripping amalgam of qualities.<br/><br/>&#39;Breakfast on Pluto&#39; is devoid of any discernible flaws, except that there is a multitude of characters to keep track of and it seems as though the film itself loses focus at times because of this, and because of a pacing that occasionally drags. A little condensation would be nice, perhaps. It also tips over into absurdity at a few points such as a maid talking to Liam Neeson&#39;s crotch (not that I didn&#39;t enjoy the close-up!) in one of Kitten&#39;s fantasies. it needs to be said: it carefully treads between stupid and fun. But it does it extremely well.<br/><br/>8 out of 10</div>\n                <div class="actions text-muted">\n                    12 out of 16 found this helpful.\n                        <span>\n        </div>\n    </div>\n            </div>\n    </div>\n</div>\n<div class="lister-item mode-detail imdb-user-review  collapsable" data-review-id="rw1470967" data-vote-url="/title/tt0411195/review/rw1470967/vote/interesting">\n    <div class="review-container">\n        <div class="lister-item-content">\n    <div class="ipl-ratings-bar">\n            <span class="rating-other-user-rating">\n            <svg class="ipl-icon ipl-star-icon  " xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" fill="#000000" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" width="24">\n                <path d="M0 0h24v24H0z" fill="none"/>\n                <path d="M12 17.27L18.18 21l-1.64-7.03L22 9.24l-7.19-.61L12 2 9.19 8.63 2 9.24l5.46 4.73L5.82 21z"/>\n                <path d="M0 0h24v24H0z" fill="none"/>\n            </svg>\n                <span>9</span><span class="point-scale">/10</span>\n            </span>\n    </div>\n<a href="/review/rw1470967/"\nclass="title" > not a planet anymore\n</a>            <div class="display-name-date">\n                    <span class="display-name-link"><a href="/user/ur4888011/"\n>lee_eisenberg</a></span><span class="review-date">9 September 2006</span>\n            </div>\n            <div class="content">\n                <div class="text show-more__control">Pluto&#39;s recent demotion from planet to &#39;dwarf planet&#39; brings to mind anything involving it, including &quot;Breakfast on Pluto&quot;. This movie does not focus on a morning meal on the former ninth planet, but on something totally different. It&#39;s about a gay Irishman (Cillian Murphy) looking for his mother in London amidst the &quot;troubles&quot; in the 1970s. The movie looks at many things: homophobia, English discrimination against - or should I say &quot;oppression of&quot; - the Irish, and Mitzi Gaynor. Watching the movie, one may feel tempted to do a number of things, namely visit Ireland and rant against the British army. And it merits much discussion about the word &quot;serious&quot;.<br/><br/>But overall, this movie isn&#39;t just about homosexuality. It&#39;s also about finding one&#39;s place in the world. And who would have ever guessed that we would see this against a background of disco and the IRA? Neil Jordan has reaffirmed himself as a dependable director. Also starring Liam Neeson, Stephen Rea and Brendan Gleeson.</div>\n                <div class="actions text-muted">\n                    7 out of 10 found this helpful.\n                        <span>\n                            Was this review helpful? <a href="/registration/signin"\n> Sign in</a> to vote.\n                        </span>\n                        <br/>\n                    <a href="/review/rw1470967/"\n>Permalink</a>\n                </div>\n            </div>\n        </div>\n        <div class="clear"></div>\n    </div>\n    <div class="gradient-expander hidden show-more">\n        <div class="gradient-container show-more__control"></div>\n            <div class="gradient-footer">\n    <div class="ipl-expander ">\n        <div class="ipl-expander__container">\n            <div class="expander-icon-wrapper show-more__control">\n                <svg class="ipl-expander__icon expander-icon " width="12" height="8" viewBox="0 0 12 8" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg">\n                     <path d="M10.197 0L6 4.304 1.803 0 0 1.85 6 8l6-6.15" fill="#2572B3" fill-rule="evenodd"/>\n                </svg>\n            </div>\n        </div>\n    </div>\n            </div>\n    </div>\n</div>\n<div class="lister-item mode-detail imdb-user-review  collapsable" data-review-id="rw1479033" data-vote-url="/title/tt0411195/review/rw1479033/vote/interesting">\n    <div class="review-container">\n        <div class="lister-item-content">\n    <div class="ipl-ratings-bar">\n            <span class="rating-other-user-rating">\n            <svg class="ipl-icon ipl-star-icon  " xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" fill="#000000" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" width="24">\n                <path d="M0 0h24v24H0z" fill="none"/>\n                <path d="M12 17.27L18.18 21l-1.64-7.03L22 9.24l-7.19-.61L12 2 9.19 8.63 2 9.24l5.46 4.73L5.82 21z"/>\n                <path d="M0 0h24v24H0z" fill="none"/>\n            </svg>\n                <span>7</span><span class="point-scale">/10</span>\n            </span>\n    </div>\n<a href="/review/rw1479033/"\nclass="title" > episodic but engrossing film\n</a>            <div class="display-name-date">\n                    <span class="display-name-link"><a href="/user/ur0375636/"\n>Buddy-51</a></span><span class="review-date">19 September 2006</span>\n            </div>\n            <div class="content">\n                <div class="text show-more__control">Based on the novel by Pat McCabe, &quot;Breakfast on Pluto&quot; takes us on a loopy journey through the turbulent years of the late 1960&#39;s and early 1970&#39;s. Our guide for the occasion is one Patrick &quot;Kitten&quot; Jordan, a hopelessly romantic transvestite who finds himself looking for love in all the wrong places.<br/><br/>The story begins in 1956 Ireland, when Patrick, as an infant, is left on the doorstep of a local priest who may just possibly be the father of the child. As Patrick grows up in the care of a bitter foster mother, he comes to learn that his real mother was a beautiful young woman - a dead ringer, he&#39;s told, for Mitzi Gaynor - who worked as a housekeeper for the priest, then disappeared in London not long after Patrick was born. With his effeminate mannerisms and penchant for wearing women&#39;s clothing, Patrick does not exactly fit into the highly conformist world of Irish Catholic society, and, as a result, he suffers much abuse at the hands of his less-than-understanding parochial school teachers who have no idea what to make of him. But Patrick has unlocked the secret to survival. He simply gives back as good as he gets, using sardonic humor and an air of indifference to protect himself from the ugliness and harshness of the society around him. Even if he is only laughing to cover up the hurt, at least it beats crying his eyes out at every bump in the road life throws his way.<br/><br/>Eventually, Patrick becomes old enough to leave home and make his own way in the world. The film relates his brief involvements with a rock-n-roll band, some IRA gun runners, and an exploitative magician, as well as his eventual journey to London to find the mother who abandoned him. While there, he has a brief stint as a streetwalker and is even arrested as the prime suspect in a dancehall firebombing. But all of these travails are just brief downpours in Patrick&#39;s life experience, and while they may dampen his mood at times, they can&#39;t extinguish his spirit.<br/><br/>Writer/director Neil Jordan has turned McCabe&#39;s novel into a fast paced (if overlong) film filled with warmth, humor and a sort of cockeyed optimism that helps to counterbalance some of the grim social issues (prejudice, child abandonment, terrorism) that lie along the story&#39;s periphery. The film occasionally feels aimless and episodic and some of Patrick&#39;s experiences are more compelling than others. Most of the subsidiary characters are left sketchy and underdeveloped, but that really doesn&#39;t matter all that much because Patrick has enough personality for the lot of them. And Cillian Murphy makes what could easily have been just another mincing gay stereotype into a multi-dimensional character of substance and depth. Most of the other actors (Liam Neeson, Stephen Rea et. al.) aren&#39;t given enough screen time to make much of an impression, though Neeson nicely underplays the role of Patrick&#39;s priest and father.<br/><br/>Patrick knows that, when the going gets tough, we all need to journey to that special place of imagination and beauty where we can find security and comfort. For Patrick, as the title suggests, that place is Pluto. However, now that that particular celestial object has lost its planetary status, I wonder if Patrick will still be traveling there to partake in the most important meal of the day.</div>\n class="lister-item mode-detail imdb-user-review  collapsable" data-review-id="rw1177785" data-vote-url="/title/tt0411195/review/rw1177785/vote/interesting">\n    <div class="review-container">\n        <div class="lister-item-content">\n    <div class="ipl-ratings-bar">\n            <span class="rating-other-user-rating">\n            <svg class="ipl-icon ipl-star-icon  " xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" fill="#000000" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" width="24">\n                <path d="M0 0h24v24H0z" fill="none"/>\n                <path d="M12 17.27L18.18 21l-1.64-7.03L22 9.24l-7.19-.61L12 2 9.19 8.63 2 9.24l5.46 4.73L5.82 21z"/>\n                <path d="M0 0h24v24H0z" fill="none"/>\n            </svg>\n                <span>9</span><span class="point-scale">/10</span>\n            </span>\n    </div>\n<a href="/review/rw1177785/"\nclass="title" > A great film that never drags...\n</a>            <div class="display-name-date">\n                    <span class="display-name-link"><a href="/user/ur2297298/"\n>hurstdragn</a></span><span class="review-date">21 September 2005</span>\n            </div>\n            <div class="content">\n                <div class="text show-more__control">I saw BOP in Toronto last week and it was one of my favorites (of the 29 I saw). Cillian Murphy was fabulous as the brave and relentless seeker of the truth who faced life with conviction even when everything around him seemed to be disintegrating. Liam Neeson as the town priest was credible and at times heartbreakingly genuine in his reactions to unfolding situations. Stephen Rea was an unorthodox but sweet magician who brought a great deal to his small part. The supporting cast, especially Brendan Gleeson and Ruth Negga, acted with realism and intensity that helped bring the film to life. Neil Jordan, whose track record stands on its own, delivered a delicious dim sum that left me wanting more and at the same time completely sated. Declan Quinn&#39;s dulcet cinematography, much like that of Monsoon Wedding and Vanity Fair, made the film one of the most lustrous at Toronto. After getting the willies watching how evil Murphy can be it was great to see him as an uber-hero. Oh, and did I say I want some of those outfits?</div>\n                <div class="actions text-muted">\n                    96 out of 132 found this helpful.\n                        <span>\n                            Was this review helpful? <a href="/registration/signin"\n> Sign in</a> to vote.\n                        </span>\n                        <br/>\n                    <a class="ipl-expander__container">\n            <div class="expander-icon-wrapper show-more__control">\n                <svg class="ipl-expander__icon expander-icon " width="12" height="8" viewBox="0 0 12 8" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg">\n                     <path d="M10.197 0L6 4.304 1.803 0 0 1.85 6 8l6-6.15" fill="#2572B3" fill-rule="evenodd"/>\n                </svg>\n            </div>\n        </div>\n    </div>\n            </div>\n    </div>\n</div>\n<div class="lister-item mode-detail imdb-user-review  with-spoiler" data-review-id="rw1185999" data-vote-url="/title/tt0411195/review/rw1185999/vote/interesting">\n    <div class="review-container">\n        <div class="lister-item-content">\n    <div class="ipl-ratings-bar">\n            <span class="rating-other-user-rating">\n            <svg class="ipl-icon ipl-star-icon  " xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" fill="#000000" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" width="24">\n                <path d="M0 0h24v24H0z" fill="none"/>\n                <path d="M12 17.27L18.18 21l-1.64-7.03L22 9.24l-7.19-.61L12 2 9.19 8.63 2 9.24l5.46 4.73L5.82 21z"/>\n                <path d="M0 0h24v24H0z" fill="none"/>\n            </svg>\n                <span>8</span><span class="point-scale">/10</span>\n            </span>\n    </div>\n<a href="/review/rw1185999/"\nclass="title" > Great Film... possible spoilers\n</a>            <div class="display-name-date">\n                    <span class="display-name-link"><a href="/user/ur6012999/"\n>DianaC224</a></span><span class="review-date">3 October 2005</span>\n            </div>\n                <span class="spoiler-warning">Warning: Spoilers</span>\n    <div class="ipl-expander ">\n        <div class="ipl-expander__container">\n            <div class="expander-icon-wrapper spoiler-warning__control">\n                <svg class="ipl-expander__icon expander-icon " width="12" height="8" viewBox="0 0 12 8" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg">\n                     <path d="M10.197 0L6 4.304 1.803 0 0 1.85 6 8l6-6.15" fill="#2572B3" fill-rule="evenodd"/>\n                </svg>\n            </div>\n        </div>\n    </div>\n            <div class="content">\n                <div class="text show-more__control">I saw the film at the NY Film Festival (with the actors in attendance), and I have to say that I loved it. In the film, Patrick &quot;Kitten&quot; Braden is an Irish baby who was abandoned by his mother on the doorstep of an uncaring stepmother. From the time he is a child, Kitten&#39;s cross dressing tendencies and his outspoken nature cause people to reject him (remember, this is Catholic Ireland in the 70s). Kitten grows up among the unrest of the IRA, but he is determined to be happy, and in order to be happy, he has to be himself (or herself). He goes to London, where he encounters all sorts of problems (they don&#39;t like the fact that he&#39;s Irish or a transvestite), but he keeps his optimistic nature despite all the hardship. The film is not about a person discovering himself (as so many coming-of-age movies are); it is about a Kitten knowing who she is and not changing her ways to please the world at large.<br/><br/>The direction and cinematography are amazing, but then this is Neil Jordan. Whatever problems you might have had with Interview With a Vampire, you can&#39;t deny that the movie was beautiful to look at. The same is true of all Jordan&#39;s films. He starts this film with a bird&#39;s eye view, and has many beautiful touches throughout. The chapter titles are hilarious. In particular, look out for the beautiful shot composition and direction of the scene between Kitten and her father in the peeping club. It&#39;s absolutely beautiful and well shot. Though he strays from the book (a lot), I believe the movie remains true to the character of Patrick, a charming, sometimes self-involved person who stubbornly makes his way through life. It must have been difficult to bring Kitten&#39;s active fantasy life to the screen, but Jordan helps us navigate between her fantasies and her reality with great skill.<br/><br/>The performances are the best thing about the film. Liam Neeson is always great, and this is no exception. Same goes for Stephen Rea. The actress who plays Charlie is someone to watch out for; she&#39;s great. The guy who plays Irwin did not impress me, but he wasn&#39;t bad. The movie, however, belongs to Cillian. Physically, he is suited for the role because he&#39;s so small, but it isn&#39;t just his appearance that helps. I&#39;ve been watching Murphy&#39;s career since 28 Days Later, and I love his ability to switch between being really intimidating (Red Eye) or really vulnerable (How Harry Became a Tree); sometimes he&#39;s both in the same movie (28 Days Later). The man knows how to use his body to convey strength, or the lack thereof. Here, he is absolutely convincing as the witty Kitten, who desperately wants to be loved, but won&#39;t compromise her personality. You can see the hurt in his eyes when he is mistreated, but also the strength of his mind when he is determined to do something (witness the gun disposal scene and the police interrogation scene). Just because Kitten looks weak doesn&#39;t mean he is weak. When you least expect it, he summons a great amount of strength to pull through difficult situations.<br/><br/>I highly recommend the movie to anyone who has a chance to see it. It is hilarious, yet heartbreaking. The events related by Kitten are sad and terrible, but Kitten&#39;s sense of humor always shines through. The audience was in stitches the whole time. Was the movie perfect? No. Is it incredibly good, even great? Definitely.</div>\n                <div class="actions text-muted">\n                    29 out of 36 found this helpful.\n                        <span>\n                            Was this review helpful? <a href="/registration/signin"\n> Sign in</a> to vote.\n                        </span>\n                        <br/>\n                    <a href="/review/rw1185999/"\n>Permalink</a>\n                </div>\n            </div>\n        </div>\n        <div class="clear"></div>\n    </div>\n</div>\n<div class="lister-item mode-detail imdb-user-review  collapsable" data-review-id="rw1287606" data-vote-url="/title/tt0411195/review/rw1287606/vote/interesting">\n    <div class="review-container">\n        <div class="lister-item-content">\n    <div class="ipl-ratings-bar">\n            <span class="rating-other-user-rating">\n            <svg class="ipl-icon ipl-star-icon  " xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" fill="#000000" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" width="24">\n                <path d="M0 0h24v24H0z" fill="none"/>\n                <path d="M12 17.27L18.18 21l-1.64-7.03L22 9.24l-7.19-.61L12 2 9.19 8.63 2 9.24l5.46 4.73L5.82 21z"/>\n                <path d="M0 0h24v24H0z" fill="none"/>\n            </svg>\n                <span>9</span><span class="point-scale">/10</span>\n            </span>\n    </div>\n<a href="/review/rw1287606/"\nclass="title" > Another triumph from Neil Jordan\n</a>            <div class="display-name-date">\n                    <span class="display-name-link"><a href="/user/ur1683855/"\n>MOscarbradley</a></span><span class="review-date">9 February 2006</span>\n            </div>\n            <div class="content">\n                <div class="text show-more__control">Of all Irish directors working internationally, (and admittedly they are few), Neil Jordan is the only one who has remained true to his roots and who has built up a body of work, often working with the same writers and actors, that could truly be said to reflect the national diaspora even when it is as fanciful as this. Jordan&#39;s vision of his native land and of those who leave it is filtered, not through a glass darkly, but through a prism. The real and surreal co-exist seamlessly. You only have to be Irish yourself and to have lived through &#39;The Troubles&#39; to understand this. My own memories of living in Northern Ireland over the past thirty years are of horrors tempered by a sense of the benign, where nothing is as bad as it seems even when it is much worse that it actually is.<br/><br/>In this extraordinary film of Pat McCabe&#39;s book that is way Patrick &#39;Kitten&#39; Brady sees the world. He is an Irish cross-dressing Candide in search of his birth mother and his adventures involve the IRA, a lonely magician, the Wombles of Wimbelton Common and working in a Soho sex club. He is almost murdered by a psychopathic punter, blown up and beaten up, (though the cop who tries to beat a confession out of him later becomes a sort of saviour to him). And through it all &#39;Kitten&#39; stoically believes in the surreal absurdity of it all. (His real father is a Catholic priest shackled by the Church&#39;s outdated celibacy laws).<br/><br/>Although adapted from Pat McCabe&#39;s novel by the director and McCabe himself the film will obviously be compared to Jordan&#39;s own original screenplay for &quot;The Crying Game&quot; with it&#39;s trans-gendered hero and the involvement of the IRA. But the similarities end there. This is a denser, all together more picaresque work. Like that other Jordan/McCabe collaboration &quot;The Butcher Boy&quot;, &#39;Kitten&#39;s&#39; view of the world is skewered by his/her over-ripe imagination just as &quot;The Butcher Boy&#39;s&quot; Francie&#39;s was, though where that ended in tragedy this ends happily.<br/><br/>From his first appearance as the adult Patrick, Cillian Murphy is hardly ever off the screen and it&#39;s a career making performance, (a close up of Murphy&#39;s face seems to allow you to know what is going on inside his head), and the supporting cast, without exception, are superb. Liam Neeson as the priest who sires him, Stephen Rea as the magician who loves him, uses him and loses him, Brendan Gleeson as an angry Womble, Gavin Friday as a gay show-band singer and a brilliant cameo from Bryan Ferry as the psychopathic punter.<br/><br/>And then there is the superb use of music from the period, some great, (Van Morrison&#39;s &#39;Madame George&#39;), some of the guilty pleasures variety. Any movie that can redeem Bobby Goldsboro&#39;s &#39;Honey&#39; and make you want to buy the best of Middle of the Road must be doing something right.</div>\n                <div class="actions text-muted">\n                    6 out of 9 found this helpful.\n                        <span>\n                            Was this review helpful? <a href="/registration/signin"\n> Sign in</a> to fill="#2572B3" fill-rule="evenodd"/>\n                </svg>\n            </div>\n        </div>\n    </div>\n            </div>\n    </div>\n</div>\n<div class="lister-item mode-detail imdb-user-review  with-spoiler" data-review-id="rw1178886" data-vote-url="/title/tt0411195/review/rw1178886/vote/interesting">\n    <div class="review-container">\n        <div class="lister-item-content">\n    <div class="ipl-ratings-bar">\n            <span class="rating-other-user-rating">\n            <svg class="ipl-icon ipl-star-icon  " xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" fill="#000000" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" width="24">\n                <path d="M0 0h24v24H0z" fill="none"/>\n                <path d="M12 17.27L18.18 21l-1.64-7.03L22 9.24l-7.19-.61L12 2 9.19 8.63 2 9.24l5.46 4.73L5.82 21z"/>\n                <path d="M0 0h24v24H0z" fill="none"/>\n            </svg>\n                <span>9</span><span class="point-scale">/10</span>\n            </span>\n    </div>\n<a href="/review/rw1178886/"\nclass="title" > More like Earth than you\'d expect\n</a>            <div class="display-name-date">\n                    <span class="display-name-link"><a href="/user/ur6761386/"\n>losdzez</a></span><span class="review-date">23 September 2005</span>\n            </div>\n                <span class="spoiler-warning">Warning: Spoilers</span>\n    <div class="ipl-expander ">\n        <div class="ipl-expander__container">\n            <div class="expander-icon-wrapper spoiler-warning__control">\n                <svg class="ipl-expander__icon expander-icon " width="12" height="8" viewBox="0 0 12 8" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg">\n                     <path d="M10.197 0L6 4.304 1.803 0 0 1.85 6 8l6-6.15" fill="#2572B3" fill-rule="evenodd"/>\n                </svg>\n            </div>\n        </div>\n    </div>\n            <div class="content">\n                <div class="text show-more__control">As the film began, my companion said &quot;Are we going to see Cillian Murphy play someone normal for once?&quot; I said &quot;No, he&#39;s playing a transvestite&quot;. I immediately wanted to take back those words, for who am I to judge someone&#39;s sexuality and/or choice of apparel . . .<br/><br/>As an infant, Kitten Brady is abandoned on the doorstep of a priest. As it turns out - beside the women&#39;s clothing and all - he&#39;s pretty normal - like anyone, he wants to know who his parents are, and why his mom left him there. He wants to belong somewhere.<br/><br/>On the one hand he seems to be drifting through life clinging to whomever will have him - but don&#39;t we all have that need to be wanted? But rather than searching for himself, Kitten is more sure of who he is than most people - he wears who he is on the outside, every day, and goes through life being bashed because of it. Most of us aren&#39;t that brave.<br/><br/>Murphy&#39;s portrayal of Kitten is flawless. (He makes a beautiful woman, by the way). He communicates Kitten&#39;s seamless connection with femininity by himself revealing nothing false about his own transformation into this character. We cease to see Kitten as a &quot;man&quot; or to define his &quot;gender&quot; somewhere in the first third of the film and instead see Kitten&#39;s feelings and longings - which are exactly like our own. He becomes familiar, comfortable. We would not begrudge Kitten being happy, ever.<br/><br/>Kitten appears weak but he&#39;s strong enough to withstand anything in his quest for belonging.<br/><br/>I found myself wanting to read the novel this movie is based on, as the IRA terrorist portion, while interesting, was a bit difficult to connect to the rest of Kitten&#39;s experience.<br/><br/>Liam Neeson is, as always, excellent, although we don&#39;t get to know his character well before we are re-introduced - so has he changed or did we just not know him? There are some nice emotional moments and we care about Kitten, but the vignettes give us more of a series of snapshots of Kitten but not much plot until the last third of the film. It left one wondering a bit if Cillian Murphy&#39;s Kitten hasn&#39;t made a sweet feast for us out of not such a filling story.<br/><br/>Still, watching this film is like eating delicious cheesecake. Each delicious bite reminds you that the last one was delicious and the next one will be delicious.</div>\n                <div class="actions text-muted">\n                    17 out of 24 found this helpful.\n                        <span>\n                            Was this review helpful? <a href="/registration/signin"\n> Sign in</a> to vote.\n                        </span>\n                        <br/>\n                    <a href="/review/rw1178886/"\n>Permalink</a>\n                </div>\n            </div>\n        </div>\n        <div class="clear"></div>\n    </div>\n</div>\n<div class="lister-item mode-detail imdb-user-review  with-spoiler" data-review-id="rw1266511" data-vote-url="/title/tt0411195/review/rw1266511/vote/interesting">\n    <div class="review-container">\n        <div class="lister-item-content">\n    <div class="ipl-ratings-bar">\n            <span class="rating-other-user-rating">\n            <svg class="ipl-icon ipl-star-icon  " xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" fill="#000000" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" width="24">\n                <path d="M0 0h24v24H0z" fill="none"/>\n                <path d="M12 17.27L18.18 21l-1.64-7.03L22 9.24l-7.19-.61L12 2 9.19 8.63 2 9.24l5.46 4.73L5.82 21z"/>\n                <path d="M0 0h24v24H0z" fill="none"/>\n            </svg>\n                <span>8</span><span class="point-scale">/10</span>\n            </span>\n    </div>\n<a href="/review/rw1266511/"\nclass="title" > Worth more than a wolf-whistle\n</a>            <div class="display-name-date">\n                    <span class="display-name-link"><a href="/user/ur0064493/"\n>Chris_Docker</a></span><span class="review-date">15 January 2006</span>\n            </div>\n                <span class="spoiler-warning">Warning: Spoilers</span>\n    <div class="ipl-expander ">\n        <div class="ipl-expander__container">\n            <div class="expander-icon-wrapper spoiler-warning__control">\n                <svg class="ipl-expander__icon expander-icon " width="12" height="8" viewBox="0 0 12 8" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg">\n                     <path d="M10.197 0L6 4.304 1.803 0 0 1.85 6 8l6-6.15" fill="#2572B3" fill-rule="evenodd"/>\n                </svg>\n            </div>\n        </div>\n    </div>\n            <div class="content">\n                <div class="text show-more__control">At once a light hearted and heart warming romp about the growing pains of Patrick (&#39;Kitten&#39;), a young transvestite, played out against a backdrop of IRA violence, and a serious contribution to the understanding gender identity, Breakfast on Pluto goes further, and allows us to look at the ways each of us develops a persona to allow our fragile inner worlds interact with a sometimes less-than-forgiving outer society. It also provides hilariously whacky touches \xc2\x96 like the two milk-stealing robins whose bird-chirrups are subtitled for our edification \xc2\x96 and the gradual oscillation between the lead character&#39;s hysterically funny debacles and asides and the more serious undercurrent fills us both with laughter and serious reflection.<br/><br/>Having &#39;Breakfast on Pluto&#39; is the culmination of Patrick&#39;s idea of perfect romance, poeticised through a life of lyricism in which the world persistently fails to come up to his inner vision. Although not all cross-dressers are transvestites, Patrick definitely wants to be a woman, swept off her feet by a strong man, soothing his worries, being a homemaker. Abandoned at birth, later adopted, suffering short shrift among the staunch Catholic community, she eventually leaves Ireland to seek her real mother who has been &#39;eaten up&#39; by the big city of London: a journey which will have an unexpected and strangely fulfilling conclusion.<br/><br/>For most of the film, the bitingly humorous dialogue extends even to life threatening situations. When Kitten is about to be executed by the IRA, she turns the tables on her assassins, berating them for arguing about who is to kill her, eventually pleading for just one bullet that they &quot;can&#39;t even spare between them&quot; and the killers leave nonplussed, making excuses about how it&#39;s not worth the bother. Later, interrogated and viciously beaten by police, she seems almost to be &#39;falling in love&#39; with her attacker in between blows, playing the devoted &#39;partner&#39; and, when the police decide they have made a mistake and forcibly eject her, begs to be allowed to remain in jail so that she can clean and be a model prisoner for them.<br/><br/>We have spent so much time laughing that it has added impact as we slowly realise that if Kitten (by her own admission) didn&#39;t spend so much time being droll she would have to cry continuously. Stepping back a moment and seeing how awful her life has become \xc2\x96 we see her as a very tough human being. Her emotional attachment to finding her real mother is parodied in scenes where a stage hypnotist gets her to believe that members of the audience and finally an inanimate object is her &#39;mother&#39;. We eventually connect with the real person beneath the colourful persona, beyond the gender identity. We see the inner radiance that has been so stymied and it even takes some of the other characters in the film beyond their stereotype prejudices. The real Patricia, freed from the threat of bigotry, social injustice and financial hardship, can blossom without so many defensive layers. The final result is breathtaking.</div>\n                <div class="actions text-muted">\n                    6 out of 9 found this helpful.\n                        <span>\n                            Was this review helpful? <a href="/registration/signin"\n> Sign in</a> to vote.\n                        </span>\n                        <br/>\n                    <a href="/review/rw1266511/"\n>Permalink</a>\n                </div>\n            </div>\n        </div>\n        <div class="clear"></div>\n    </div>\n</div>\n<div class="lister-item mode-detail imdb-user-review  collapsable" data-review-id="rw1216039" data-vote-url="/title/tt0411195/review/rw1216039/vote/interesting">\n    <div class="review-container">\n        <div class="lister-item-content">\n    <div class="ipl-ratings-bar">\n            <span class="rating-other-user-rating">\n            <svg class="ipl-icon ipl-star-icon  " xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" fill="#000000" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" width="24">\n                <path d="M0 0h24v24H0z" fill="none"/>\n                <path d="M12 17.27L18.18 21l-1.64-7.03L22 9.24l-7.19-.61L12 2 9.19 8.63 2 9.24l5.46 4.73L5.82 21z"/>\n                <path d="M0 0h24v24H0z" fill="none"/>\n            </svg>\n                <span>10</span><span class="point-scale">/10</span>\n            </span>\n    </div>\n<a href="/review/rw1216039/"\nclass="title" > The best film of the year by far!\n</a>            <div class="display-name-date">\n                    <span class="display-name-link"><a href="/user/ur7991196/"\n>morrellally</a></span><span class="review-date">14 November 2005</span>\n            </div>\n            <div class="content">\n                <div class="text show-more__control">I have now seen this film twice, and I think it is the year&#39;s best film by far. Cillian Murphy performance is absolutely astonishing. He should get an Oscar for sure. Both of the viewings I went to for this film were followed by a standing ovation, and lots of tears from many audience members. It is a modern day fairy tale, told in the most devastatingly beautiful way. can honestly not say enough good things about this film, and especially Cillian Murphy&#39;s performance. I personally have never been touched by a film like I have by this one. There is so much honesty, love and innocence. It is absolutely beautiful. I Please go see this film. It is truly an incredible experience.</div>\n                <div class="actions text-muted">\n                    75 out of 103 found this helpful.\n                        <span>\n
